B00132D808|4.0|The wait is finally over. It's been three years since Panic At The Disco, the exclamation point optional, released their debut album, A Fever You Can't Sweat Out. The band since then has grown and is headlining this years Honda Civic Tour with The Hush Sound, Motion City Soundtrack, and Phantom Planet. On March 25th, the band's sophomore album, Pretty.Odd (the punctuation never ends with these boys), was released. Let's say it was definitely a huge thing for their fans. On January 28th, the pre-order on Fueled By Ramen's, their record label, website was available and you had to wait at least five minutes for you even to be able to checkout. I know this from experience, no need to say that Panic At the Disco broke the internet that day.       Now if you don't know who Panic At The Disco is, don't know how you don't, \\"I Write Sins, Not Tragedies\\" got so much air time there's no way you wouldn't recognize it you heard it. Anyways, Panic At the Disco consists of four very young guys. There's Ryan Ross who writes most of the lyrics, plays guitar and sings. Brendon Urie who's the lead singer, also plays piano and guitar. Then of course Jon Walker the bassist and Spencer Smith on drums. Basically they contacted Pete Wentz of Fall Out Boy who flew out to Las Vegas to meet them and they were signed to Decaydance/Fueled By Ramen.     They tell us that they've been writing songs for us, and they sure have been. The album starts off with a song called \\"We're So Starving\\". They tell us in the song that \\"You don't have to worry because we're still the same band,\\", for the most part that is true, yet lies, well, the only lie is that Jon Walker wasn't on the first album, otherwise, it's correct. The song does have a nice flow to it and it starts the album of on a good note. It leads into the next song \\"Nine in the Afternoon\\", the album's first single. \\"Nine in the Afternoon\\" brings a different side to Panic. Big horns and orchestra-like sounds. The song definitely stands out on thealbum, there really isn't another song like it. There is a calming outro at the end. At the same time, it stands out weirdly from the rest of the song, these nice, quiet strings. But I think that it leads well into the rest of the album, telling you \\"this isn't going quite where you think it is.\\" Next comes \\"She's a Handsome Women\\" as Panic continues with they're unique song titles. If you listen closely to the parts, the bass in this song is way more complex than the guitar, it's very amusing. \\"Don't You Know What I'm Seeing\\" seems to stand out as one of the favorites. There's sort-of sad lyrics hiding inside this song, and yet it makes me feel happy? Panic Magic? Who knows. I like the idea that life goes on, with or without you, and all you can hope is that the one you love goes with you. The weather doesn't give a damn about you at all. I didn't hear the bird noises at first, but they entertain me. And Spencer's in the back being subtly awesome, and it makes me happy. This song is eminently singable, and I already know all the words. I think it's kind of my stealth favorite. \\"That Green Gentleman (Things Have Changed)\\" is the second single from this album (yet to be released). It's about how things can change you, even though you still feel like the same person, until suddenly you see how far you've come without realizing it.  It's definitely a good choice for the second single. \\"I Have Friends In Holy Places\\", there's ukulele, clarinets and Brendon Urie, well, he's a given. This song makes me smile all over my face, because it's adorable. This is jazzy and wild and lovely, and it's so NOT mainstream it makes me cry with joy. I suspect that a lot of Fever fans are going to hate it, but I don't know why because something about it reminds me of Better If You Do, so much so that on a mix I would probably put them next to each other. But at the end, the little outro feels almost like a melancholic echo, like the first part was a memory. The end of the songs brings you into the next song \\"Northern Downpour\\". The song would definitely be a good example of how the band sounds now, even though Ryan Ross believes that another song is, but, we'll get to that later. Ryan's voice being a real presence, and matched equally with Brendon's. Just the four of them, without too many bells and whistles, and a laid-back feeling that makes me think of warm spring days (funny, since they talk about a downpour...)         The next song is \\"When The Day Met The Night\\". This track is like Beatles music covered by The Polyphonic Spree, baked into a cupcake and iced with pure joy. How can you go wrong with a love song about the sun and the moon and bright chorus contrasts. The chorus versus the verses in this song is amazing - the verses are almost more melancholy, despite not being so lyrically, but the chorus is bright and happy. I love it. \\"Pas de Cheval\\" comes next. Now this is a song where you shouldn't judge the song by it's name because the song is nothing short of amazing. \\"The Piano Knows Something I Don't\\",In their MTV interview, Ryan calls this one experimental, so... news flash: the experiment was a success. I really dig the bookend feel to this, a little manic-almost-forced-feeling happiness shoehorned in between haunting little snippets that are not only melancholy, but are actually allowed to be.  I love the contrasts in this song of the intro/outro vs. the middle. The very quiet versus the the very bouncy, it is amazing and I adore it ridiculously. It brings a lot of interest to the song. \\"Behind the Sea\\" brings Ryan Ross singing lead vocals. Before hearing this version, I had heard the acoustic version. There's something really melancholy and beautiful in that version, and it exists here too, but it's carried along by the tempo and the rest of the instrumentation, almost as if our little melancholy songwriter is carried along with the tide of life being not-so-bad-today. (If I can get meta for a minute, this is probably the very best example of how Ryan's strange, sometimes overly maudlin lyrics become something completely different when they're incorporated into and augmented by the rest of the band. Fever was Ryan and a laptop, but Pretty is Ryan and Brendon and Spencer and Jon in a studio as a band. If Pretty's got a parade track, a Yellow Submarine track, this is it. The outro at the end is... odd compared to the rest of the song. I like it, but it's just. Odd.     \\"Folkin' Around\\". This is the one song I can talk forever about. It was written by Brendon Urie. This song is all Brendon. The number one thing I learned from this song is how much I love Brendon Urie. The number two thing I learned is how much I want him to do a song with Nickel Creek. (Or for Ryan to play more mandolin, I guess.) There's been rumors that this song has to do with his parents, and I don't know if that's based on anything that Brendon's said, or if others (like me) can spot \\"you suck Dad\\" lyrics a mile off. There's this attitude that Brendon has projected through the lyrics thats basically \\"forget everyone\\". For example: \\"And I'll even have the courtesy of admitting I was wrong / As the final words before I'm dead and gone\\", directed to the lover in the song or symbolically to someone else. I'm putting out the lantern, I'm not waiting for you anymore, you can find your own way back to me. There's a youth and a fragility in his voice that belies his nimble singing and the perky feel of the track.  Also, I just think it's really funny that Ryan, King of the Bizarre Metaphor (\\"aubergine dreams,\\" people!) \\"didn't get\\" this song at first.     \\"She Had The World\\" comes next. This is, like, a minstrel waltz, and I don't even know what to do with that. It's a backwards minstrel waltz, because it's not about the singer's love not loving him back, but about the singer not loving the lover.  It's incredibly beautiful and charming and mainstream radio is just going 'what are we going to do with this' and throwing up its hands. Next comes \\"From A Mountain in the Middle of the Cabins\\". Jon calls this one an outro for the feel of the record, and I think that's really true. But I also kinda think it's maybe a little bit of a goodbye to Fever, and their Vaudeville act. Maybe that's just the saloon piano and my own screwed-up logic talking. (How is it that Panic writes a song about a breakup and it makes me want to bounce in my seat and do a little soft shoe? I Do Not Know. If I ever meet Ryan, this is what I will ask him. (That, and where he gets his scarves.) Moving on. \\"Mad as Rabbits\\" closes the album. There is nothing that is not crazy and awesome about this song. This one would be interested paired with Nine In The Afternoon, especially for the video. The way Brendon sings \\"when I was a bird and you were a map!\\" reminds me of a Muppet, and I do not know why. (Brendon Urie = secretly created by Jim Henson?) Spencer, once again is in the back being subtly awesome. Ryan's really asserted himself as a regular vocalist in their band.. I kind of hope that Mad As Rabbits becomes a bit of a jam song, because I actually think that a little jam band mentality would go well with their new sound. I'm not talking Inna Gadda Davida, here, but there's room in the bridge for some extended solo work. Certainly they've got the chops for it.    In many other reviews Pretty.Odd has been called \\"copy of the Beatles\\" or just Beatles-esque. I definitely disagree with this. Panic has shown that they've improved their sound, bringing a whole new style to their music. So, definitely pick up a copy because this ish is Bananas. No, seriously, it is.

1401200605|5.0|Jeph Loeb writes comics like summer movie blockbusters with a galaxy of stars. These movies, or comics, can be fun but may lack substance. In Hush we have an action packed story with a parade of guest stars, heroes and villains alike. Are their appearances mainly to add star power? Possibly. Do they add to the enjoyment of the story? Definately. This is no different from his previous sagas Long Halloween and Dark Victory. One thing is certain, with Jim Lee as cinematographer/artist, they have never looked better. Batman's always been a top leading man and remains a draw. As leading lady we have Catwoman, Poison Ivy is the temptress, Talia al Ghul the femme fatale. Add the Joker, Harley Quinn, Clayface, Harvey Dent, Killer Croc, Huntress, Scarecrow, Nightwing, Superman, Lois Lane ...whew, talk about a big budget flick. Here lies many of the barbs hurled at Hush.  Some criticize it as a visual tour de force by the great Jim Lee and nothing more than eye candy. The plot has flaws. The reveal of the antagonist is a foregone conclusion and his motivations for becoming Hush are dubious, but now we're missing the point. This isn't about reason or logic. For fans of that there are better choices and to demand it here is being a stick in the mud. This story is all about fun, and in the context of movie blockbusters it's a complete and total success.
